# §1101

* * *

[[1]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002000-ref) See References in Text note below.

[[2]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002001-ref) So in original. The words “the[alien”](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) probably should not appear.

[[3]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002002-ref) See Availability of Funds note below.

[[4]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002003-ref) So in original. Probably should be followed by “; or”.

[[5]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002004-ref) So in original. Probably should be preceded by “is”.

[[6]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002005-ref) So in original. Probably should be followed by a semicolon.

[[7]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#fn002006-ref) So in original. The phrase “of such section” probably should not appear.

Amendment of Subsection (a)(15)(H)(i)

For termination of amendment by [section 107(c) of Pub. L. 108–77](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._108-77), see Effective and Termination Dates of 2003 Amendment note below.

**Editorial Notes**

References in Text

This chapter, referred to in subsecs. (a), (b) (except par. (1)(G)(ii)), (c), and (e)–(g), was in the original, “this Act”, meaning act June 27, 1952, ch. 477, [66 Stat. 163](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/66_Stat._163), known as the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act), which is classified principally to this chapter. For complete classification of this Act to the Code, see Short Title note set out below and Tables.

The Headquarters Agreement with the United Nations ([61 Stat. 758](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/61_Stat._758)), referred to in subsec. (a)(15)(C)(ii), is set out as a note under [section 287 of Title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/287), Foreign Relations and Intercourse.

[Section 1184(l) of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1184#l), referred to in subsec. (a)(15)(F)(i), probably means the subsec. (l) of section 1184 which relates to nonimmigrant elementary and secondary school students and was added by [Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title VI, § 625(a)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–699](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-699), and redesignated subsec. (m) of section 1184 by [Pub. L. 106–386, div. A, § 107(e)(2)(A)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-386), Oct. 28, 2000, [114 Stat. 1478](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1478).

The [International Organizations Immunities Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/international_organizations_immunities_act) ([59 Stat. 669](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/59_Stat._669)), referred to in subsec. (a)(15)(G)(i), is act Dec. 29, 1945, ch. 652, title I, [59 Stat. 669](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/59_Stat._669), which is classified principally to subchapter XVIII (§ 288 et seq.) of chapter 7 of Title 22, Foreign Relations and Intercourse. For complete classification of this Act to the Code, see Short Title note set out under [section 288 of Title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/288) and Tables.

Subsection (p) of [section 1184 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1184), referred to in subsec. (a)(15)(K), was redesignated as subsec. (r) of section 1184 by [Pub. L. 108–193, § 8(a)(3)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._108-193), Dec. 19, 2003, [117 Stat. 2886](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/117_Stat._2886).

Section 3(a) of the [Selective Training and Service Act of 1940](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/burke-wadsworth_act), as amended ([54 Stat. 885](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/54_Stat._885); [55 Stat. 844](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/55_Stat._844)), referred to in subsec. (a)(19), was classified to section 303 of the former [Appendix to Title 50](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/50a), War and[National](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)Defense, and was omitted from the Code as obsolete.

The [Selective Service Act of 1948](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/military_selective_service_act), referred to in subsec. (a)(19), was redesignated the [Universal Military Training and Service Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/military_selective_service_act) by act June 19, 1951, [65 Stat. 75](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/65_Stat._75), and then redesignated the [Military Selective Service Act of 1967](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/military_selective_service_act) by act June 30, 1967, [Pub. L. 90–40](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._90-40), [81 Stat. 100](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/81_Stat._100), and subsequently redesignated the [Military Selective Service Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/military_selective_service_act) by [Pub. L. 92–129, title I, § 101(a)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._92-129), Sept. 28, 1971, [85 Stat. 348](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/85_Stat._348).

The [Immigration Technical Corrections Act of 1988](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_technical_corrections_act_of_1988), referred to in subsec. (a)(27)(L)(iii), is [Pub. L. 100–525](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._100-525), Oct. 24, 1988, [102 Stat. 2609](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/102_Stat._2609). For complete classification of this Act to the Code, see Short Title of 1988 Amendments note set out below and Tables.

The [Immigration and Nationality Technical Corrections Act of 1994](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_technical_corrections_act_of_1994), referred to in subsec. (a)(27)(L)(iii), is [Pub. L. 103–416](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._103-416), Oct. 25, 1994, [108 Stat. 4305](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/108_Stat._4305). For complete classification of this Act to the Code, see Short Title of 1994 Amendment note set out below and Tables.

The [American Competitiveness and Workforce Improvement Act of 1998](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/american_competitiveness_and_workforce_improvement_act_of_1998), referred to in subsec. (a)(27)(L)(iii), is [Pub. L. 105–277, div. C, title IV](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-277), Oct. 21, 1998, [112 Stat. 2681–641](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/112_Stat._2681-641). For complete classification of this Act to the Code, see Short Title of 1998 Amendment note set out below and Tables.

Section 902(d)(1)(B) of the [Haitian Refugee Immigration Fairness Act of 1998](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/haitian_refugee_immigration_fairness_act_of_1998), referred to in subsec. (a)(51)(E), is [Pub. L. 105–277, div. A, § 101(h) [title IX, § 902(d)(1)(B)]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-277), which is set out as a note under [section 1255 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255).

Section 202(d)(1) of the [Nicaraguan Adjustment and Central American Relief Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/nicaraguan_adjustment_and_central_american_relief_act), referred to in subsec. (a)(51)(F), is [section 202(d)(1) of Pub. L. 105–100](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-100), which is set out as a note under [section 1255 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255).

Section 309 of the Illegal Immigration Reform and [Immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) Responsibility Act of 1996, referred to in subsec. (a)(51)(G), is [section 309 of div. C of Pub. L. 104–208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), which is set out as a note under this section.

[Section 1432 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1432), referred to in subsec. (c)(1), was repealed by [Pub. L. 106–395, title I, § 103(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-395), Oct. 30, 2000, [114 Stat. 1632](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1632).

Codification

September 30, 1996, referred to in the concluding provisions of subsec. (a)(43), was in the original “the date of enactment of this paragraph”, which was translated as meaning the date of enactment of [section 321(b) of Pub. L. 104–208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), which inserted that language, to reflect the probable intent of Congress.

Amendments

2023—Subsec. (a)(15)(C). [Pub. L. 117–360, § 2(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-360), amended subpar. (C) generally. Prior to amendment, subpar. (C) read as follows: “an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)in immediate and continuous transit through the[United States,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) or an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who qualifies as a[person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=)entitled to pass in transit to and from the United Nations Headquarters District and foreign countries, under the provisions of paragraphs (3), (4), and (5) of section 11 of the Headquarters Agreement with the United Nations ([61 Stat. 758](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/61_Stat._758));”.

Subsec. (a)(15)(D)(iii). [Pub. L. 117–360, § 2(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-360), added cl. (iii).

Subsec. (a)(15)(E). [Pub. L. 117–263, § 5902(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-263), inserted “(or, in the case of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who acquired the relevant nationality through a financial investment and who has not previously been granted status under this subparagraph, the[foreign state](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1597347259-1201680035&term_occur=999&term_src=)of which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is a[national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)and in which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)has been domiciled for a continuous period of not less than 3 years at any point before applying for a[nonimmigrant visa](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=)under this subparagraph)” before “, and the spouse”, substituted “such[alien”](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) for “him”, and substituted “the[alien”](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) for “he” wherever appearing.

**Statutory Notes and Related Subsidiaries**

Change of Name

Broadcasting Board of Governors renamed[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Agency for Global Media pursuant to [section 6204(a)(21) of Title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/6204#a_21), Foreign Relations and Intercourse. The renaming was effectuated by notice to congressional appropriations committees dated May 24, 2018, and became effective Aug. 22, 2018.

Effective Date of 2010 Amendment

[Pub. L. 111–306, § 1(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._111-306), Dec. 14, 2010, [124 Stat. 3280](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/124_Stat._3280), provided that:

“(1) In general.—Except as provided in paragraph (2), the amendments made by subsection (a) [amending this section] shall—

“(A)

take effect on the date that is 180 days after the date of the enactment of this Act [Dec. 14, 2010]; and

“(2) Temporary exception.—

“(A) In general.—

Notwithstanding section 101(a)(15)(F)(i) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act), as amended by subsection (a), during the 3-year period beginning on the date of the enactment of this Act, an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)seeking to enter the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)to pursue a course of study at a language training program that has been certified by the Secretary of Homeland Security and has not been accredited or denied accreditation by an entity described in section 101(a)(52) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(52)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_52)] may be granted a[nonimmigrant visa](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=)under such section 101(a)(15)(F)(i).

“(B) Additional requirement.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) may not be granted a [nonimmigrant visa](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=) under subparagraph (A) if the sponsoring institution of the language training program to which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)seeks to enroll does not—

“(i)

submit an application for the accreditation of such program to a regional or [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) accrediting agency recognized by the Secretary of Education within 1 year after the date of the enactment of this Act; and

“(ii)

comply with the applicable accrediting requirements of such agency.”

[Pub. L. 111–287, § 4](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._111-287), Nov. 30, 2010, [124 Stat. 3059](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/124_Stat._3059), provided that:

“(a) In General.—

Except as provided in subsection (b), the amendments made by this Act [amending this section and [section 1182 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182)] shall take effect on the date of the enactment of this Act [Nov. 30, 2010].

A, § 101(b) [title IV, § 410(c)]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-277), Oct. 21, 1998, [112 Stat. 2681–50](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/112_Stat._2681-50), 2681–104; [Pub. L. 107–173, title VI, § 601](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._107-173), May 14, 2002, [116 Stat. 564](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/116_Stat._564), provided that:

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title III, § 309](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–625](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-625), as amended by [Pub. L. 104–302, § 2(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-302), (3), Oct. 11, 1996, [110 Stat. 3657](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3657); [Pub. L. 105–100, title II](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-100), §§ 203(a)–(c), 204(d), Nov. 19, 1997, [111 Stat. 2196–2199](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/111_Stat._2196-2199), 2201; [Pub. L. 105–139, § 1(c)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-139), Dec. 2, 1997, [111 Stat. 2644](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/111_Stat._2644); [Pub. L. 106–386, div. B, title V](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-386), §§ 1506(b)(3), 1510(b), Oct. 28, 2000, [114 Stat. 1527](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1527), 1531; [Pub. L. 106–554, § 1(a)(4) [div. B, title XV, § 1505(c)]](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-554), Dec. 21, 2000, [114 Stat. 2763](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._2763), 2763A–327, provided that:

“(a) In General.—

Except as provided in this section and sections [303(b)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/303#b_2), [306(c)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/306#c), [308(d)(2)(D)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/308#d_2_D), or [308(d)(5)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/308#d_5) of this division [amending sections [1225](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1225), [1227](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1227), and [1251](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1251) of this title, enacting provisions set out as notes under sections [1225](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1225), [1226](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1226), [1227](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1227), and [1252](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1252) of this title, and repealing provisions set out as a note under [section 1225 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1225)], this subtitle [subtitle A (§§ 301–309) of title III of div. C of [Pub. L. 104–208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), see Tables for classification] and the amendments made by this subtitle shall take effect on the first day of the first month beginning more than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 1996] (in this title [see Tables for classification] referred to as the ‘title III–A effective date’).

“(b) Promulgation of Regulations.—

The [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall first promulgate regulations to carry out this subtitle by not later than 30 days before the title III–A effective date.

“(c) Transition for Certain Aliens.—

“(1) General rule that new rules do not apply.—Subject to the succeeding provisions of this subsection, in the case of an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who is in exclusion or deportation proceedings before the title III–A effective date—

“(A)

the amendments made by this subtitle shall not apply, and

“(B)

the proceedings (including judicial review thereof) shall continue to be conducted without regard to such amendments.

“(2) Attorney general option to elect to apply new procedures.—

In a case described in paragraph (1) in which an evidentiary hearing under section 236 or 242 and 242B of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1226](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1226), 1252, former 1252b] has not commenced as of the title III–A effective date, the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may elect to proceed under chapter 4 of title II of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1221](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1221) et seq.] (as amended by this subtitle). The[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall provide notice of such election to the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)involved not later than 30 days before the date any evidentiary hearing is commenced. If the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)makes such election, the notice of hearing provided to the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)under section 235 or 242(a) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1225](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1225), 1252(a)] shall be valid as if provided under section 239 of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1229](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229)] (as amended by this subtitle) to confer jurisdiction on the[immigration judge.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1496754849-1485255819&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(3) Attorney general option to terminate and reinitiate proceedings.—

In the case described in paragraph (1), the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) may elect to terminate proceedings in which there has not been a final administrative decision and to reinitiate proceedings under chapter 4 of title II [of] the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1221](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1221) et seq.] (as amended by this subtitle). Any determination in the terminated proceeding shall not be binding in the reinitiated proceeding.

“(4) Transitional changes in judicial review.—In the case in which a final order of exclusion or deportation is entered more than 30 days after the date of the enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 1996], notwithstanding any provision of section 106 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [former [8 U.S.C. 1105a](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1105a)] (as in effect as of the date of the enactment of this Act) to the contrary—

“(A)

in the case of judicial review of a final order of exclusion, subsection (b) of such section shall not apply and the action for judicial review shall be governed by the provisions of subsections (a) and (c) of such [section] in the same manner as they apply to judicial review of orders of deportation;

“(C)

the petition for judicial review must be filed not later than 30 days after the date of the final order of exclusion or deportation;

“(D)

the petition for review shall be filed with the court of appeals for the judicial circuit in which the administrative proceedings before the special inquiry officer or [immigration judge](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1496754849-1485255819&term_occur=999&term_src=) were completed;

“(E)

there shall be no appeal of any discretionary decision under section 212(c), 212(h), 212(i), 244, or 245 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8) former 1182(c), 1182(h), (i), former 1254, 1255] (as in effect as of the date of the enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 1996]);

“(F)

[service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) of the petition for review shall not stay the deportation of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)pending the court’s decision on the petition, unless the court orders otherwise; and

“(G)

there shall be no appeal permitted in the case of an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who is inadmissible or deportable by reason of having committed a criminal offense covered in section 212(a)(2) or section 241(a)(2)(A)(iii), (B), (C), or (D) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1182(a)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182#a_2), former 1251(a)(2)(A)(iii), (B), (C), (D)] (as in effect as of the date of the enactment of this Act), or any offense covered by section 241(a)(2)(A)(ii) of such Act (as in effect on such date) for which both predicate offenses are, without regard to their date of commission, otherwise covered by section 241(a)(2)(A)(i) of such Act (as so in effect).

“(5) Transitional rules with regard to suspension of deportation.—

“(B) Exception for certain orders.—

In any case in which the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) elects to terminate and reinitiate proceedings in accordance with paragraph (3) of this subsection, paragraphs (1) and (2) of section 240A(d) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1229b(d)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229b#d_1), (2)] shall not apply to an order to show cause issued before April 1, 1997.

“(C) Special rule for certain aliens granted temporary protection from deportation and for battered spouses and children.—

“(i) In general.—For purposes of calculating the period of continuous physical presence under section 244(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [former [8 U.S.C. 1254(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1254#a)] (as in effect before the title III–A effective date) or section 240A of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1229b](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229b)] (as in effect after the title III–A effective date), subparagraph (A) of this paragraph and paragraphs (1) and (2) of section 240A(d) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) shall not apply in the case of an[alien,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) regardless of whether the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is in exclusion or deportation proceedings before the title III–A effective date, who has not been convicted at any time of an[aggravated felony](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2031923285-1201680127&term_occur=999&term_src=)(as defined in section 101(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a)]) and—

“(I) was not apprehended after December 19, 1990, at the time of entry, and is—

“(aa)

a Salvadoran [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) who first entered the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) on or before September 19, 1990, and who registered for benefits pursuant to the settlement agreement in American Baptist Churches, et al. v. Thornburgh (ABC), 760 F. Supp. 796 (N.D. Cal. 1991) on or before October 31, 1991, or applied for temporary protected status on or before October 31, 1991; or

“(bb)

a Guatemalan [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) who first entered the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) on or before October 1, 1990, and who registered for benefits pursuant to such settlement agreement on or before December 31, 1991;

“(II)

is a Guatemalan or Salvadoran [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) who filed an application for asylum with the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)on or before April 1, 1990;

“(III)

is the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) (as defined in section 101(b)(1) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101(b)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#b_1)]) of an individual, at the time a decision is rendered to suspend the deportation, or cancel the removal, of such individual, if the individual has been determined to be described in this clause (excluding this subclause and subclause (IV));

“(IV) is the [unmarried](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1743703365-1201680102&term_occur=999&term_src=) son or daughter of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)parent, at the time a decision is rendered to suspend the deportation, or cancel the removal, of such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)parent, if—

“(aa)

the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) parent has been determined to be described in this clause (excluding this subclause and subclause (III)); and

“(bb)

in the case of a son or daughter who is 21 years of age or older at the time such decision is rendered, the son or daughter entered the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) on or before October 1, 1990;

“(V)

is an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who entered the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) on or before December 31, 1990, who filed an application for asylum on or before December 31, 1991, and who, at the time of filing such application, was a[national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the Soviet Union, Russia, any republic of the former Soviet Union, Latvia, Estonia, Lithuania, Poland, Czechoslovakia, Romania, Hungary, Bulgaria, Albania, East Germany, Yugoslavia, or any[state](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the former Yugoslavia; or

“(VI)

is an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who was issued an order to show cause or was in deportation proceedings before April 1, 1997, and who applied for suspension of deportation under section 244(a)(3) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [former [8 U.S.C. 1254(a)(3)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1254#a_3)] (as in effect before the date of the enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 1996]); or

“(VII)

(aa) was the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subclause (I), (II), or (V)—

“(AA)

at the time at which a decision is rendered to suspend the deportation or cancel the removal of the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=);

“(BB)

at the time at which the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) filed an application for suspension of deportation or cancellation of removal; or

“(CC)

at the time at which the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) registered for benefits under the settlement agreement in American Baptist Churches, et. al. v. Thornburgh (ABC), applied for temporary protected status, or applied for asylum; and

“(bb)

the spouse, [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=), or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of the spouse has been battered or subjected to extreme cruelty by the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subclause (I), (II), or (V).

“(ii) Limitation on judicial review.—

A determination by the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) as to whether an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)satisfies the requirements of clause (i) is final and shall not be subject to review by any court. Nothing in the preceding sentence shall be construed as limiting the application of section 242(a)(2)(B) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1252(a)(2)(B)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1252#a_2_B)] (as in effect after the title III–A effective date) to other eligibility determinations pertaining to discretionary relief under this Act [probably should be “division”, see Short Title of 1996 Amendment note below].

“(iv) Residence with spouse or parent not required.—

For purposes of the application of clause (i)(VII), a spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall not be required to demonstrate that he or she is residing with the spouse or parent in the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(7) Limitation on suspension of deportation.—

After April 1, 1997, the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may not suspend the deportation and adjust the status under section 244 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [former [8 U.S.C. 1254](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1254)] (as in effect before the title III–A effective date) of any[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)in any fiscal year, except in accordance with section 240A(e) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1229b(e)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229b#e)]. The previous sentence shall apply regardless of when an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)applied for such suspension and adjustment.

“(d) Transitional References.—For purposes of carrying out the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101) et seq.], as amended by this subtitle—

“(1)

any reference in section 212(a)(1)(A) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1182(a)(1)(A)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182#a_1_A)] to the term ‘inadmissible’ is deemed to include a reference to the term ‘excludable’, and

“(2)

any reference in law to an order of removal shall be deemed to include a reference to an order of exclusion and deportation or an [order of deportation](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-166357500-1201680131&term_occur=999&term_src=).

“(e) Transition.—

No period of time before the date of the enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 1996] shall be included in the period of 1 year described in section 212(a)(6)(B)(i) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1182(a)(6)(B)(i)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182#a_6_B_i)] (as amended by section 301(c) of this division).

“(f) Special Rule for Cancellation of Removal.—

“(1) In general.—Subject to the provisions of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101) et seq.] (as in effect after the title III–A effective date), other than subsections (b)(1), (d)(1), and (e) of section 240A of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1229b(b)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229b#b_1), (d)(1), (e)] (but including section 242(a)(2)(B) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1252(a)(2)(B)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1252#a_2_B)]), the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may, under section 240A of such Act, cancel removal of, and adjust to the status of an alien[lawfully admitted for permanent residence,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2124716147-1201680062&term_occur=999&term_src=) an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who is inadmissible or deportable from the[United States,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) if the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)applies for such relief, the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is described in subsection (c)(5)(C)(i) of this section, and—

“(A) the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(ii)

has been physically present in the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) for a continuous period of not less than 7 years immediately preceding the date of such application;

“(iii)

has been a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) of good moral character during such period; and

“(B) the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(iii)

has been physically present in the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) for a continuous period of not less than 10 years immediately following the commission of an act, or the assumption of a status, constituting a ground for removal;

“(iv)

has been a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) of good moral character during such period; and

“(2) Treatment of certain breaks in presence.—

Section 240A(d)(2) [[8 U.S.C. 1229b(d)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1229b#d_2)] shall apply for purposes of calculating any period of continuous physical presence under this subsection, except that the reference to subsection (b)(1) in such section shall be considered to be a reference to paragraph (1) of this section.

“(h) Relief and Motions to Reopen.—

“(1) Relief.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in subsection (c)(5)(C)(i) who is otherwise eligible for—

“(2) Additional motion to reopen permitted.—

Notwithstanding any limitation imposed by law on motions to reopen removal or deportation proceedings (except limitations premised on an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)’s [conviction](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2143927138-1201680132&term_occur=999&term_src=) of an [aggravated felony](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2031923285-1201680127&term_occur=999&term_src=) (as defined by section 101(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a)])), any[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who is described in subsection (c)(5)(C)(i) and who has become eligible for cancellation of removal or suspension of deportation as a result of the enactment of paragraph (1) may file one motion to reopen removal or deportation proceedings in order to apply for cancellation of removal or suspension of deportation. The scope of any proceeding reopened on this basis shall be limited to a determination of the[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s eligibility for cancellation of removal or suspension of deportation. The[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall designate a specific time period in which all such motions to reopen are required to be filed. The period shall begin not later than 60 days after the date of the enactment of this subsection [Dec. 21, 2000] and shall extend for a period not to exceed 240 days.

“(a) In General.—

“(2)

Section 104 [amending sections [1157](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157) and [1159](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1159) of this title and enacting provisions set out as notes under [section 1159 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1159)] (relating to asylee adjustments).

Section 162(b) [amending [section 1154 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1154)] (relating to[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visa petitioning process), but only insofar as such section relates to visas for fiscal years beginning with fiscal year 1992.

“(c) General Transitions.—

“(1) In the case of a petition filed under section 204(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1154(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1154#a)] before October 1, 1991, for preference status under section 203(a)(3) or section 203(a)(6) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1153(a)(3)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153#a_3), (6)] (as in effect before such date)—

“(A)

in order to maintain the priority date with respect to such a petition, the petitioner must file (by not later than October 1, 1993) a new petition for classification of the employment under paragraph (1), (2), or (3) of section 203(b) of such Act (as amended by this title), and

“(B)

any labor certification under section 212(a)(5)(A) of such Act required with respect to the new petition shall be deemed approved if the labor certification with respect to the previous petition was previously approved under section 212(a)(14) of such Act.

In the case of a petition filed under section 204(a) of such Act before October 1, 1991, but which is not described in paragraph (4), and for which a filing fee was paid, any additional filing fee shall not exceed one-half of the fee for the filing of the new petition referred to in subparagraph (A).

“(2)

Any petition filed under section 204(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) before October 1, 1991, for preference status under section 203(a)(4) or section 203(a)(5) of such Act (as in effect before such date) shall be deemed, as of such date, to be a petition filed under such section for preference status under section 203(a)(3) or section 203(a)(4), respectively, of such Act (as amended by this title).

“(3)

In the case of an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who is described in section 203(a)(8) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) (as in effect before October 1, 1991) as the spouse or[child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=)of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)admitted for[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)residence as a preference[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)under section 203(a)(3) or 203(a)(6) of such Act (as in effect before such date) and who would be entitled to enter the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)under such section 203(a)(8) but for the amendments made by this title [see subsec. (a) above], such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall be deemed to be described in section 203(d) of such Act as the spouse or[child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=)of an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in section 203(b)(2) or 203(b)(3)(A)(i), respectively, of such Act with the same priority date as that of the principal[alien.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(4)

(A)

Subject to subparagraph (B), any petition filed before October 1, 1991, and approved on any date, to accord status under section 203(a)(3) or 203(a)(6) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) (as in effect before such date) shall be deemed, on and after October 1, 1991 (or, if later, the date of such approval), to be a petition approved to accord status under section 203(b)(2) or under the appropriate classification under section 203(b)(3), respectively, of such Act (as in effect on and after such date). Nothing in this subparagraph shall be construed as exempting the beneficiaries of such petitions from the numerical limitations under section 203(b)(2) or 203(b)(3) of such Act.

“(B)

Subparagraph (A) shall not apply more than two years after the date the priority date for issuance of a visa on the basis of such a petition has been reached.

“(a)

Except as provided in subsections (b) and (c), this title and the amendments made by this title [enacting sections [1157](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157), [1158](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1158), and [1159](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1159) of this title, amending this section and sections [1151](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1151) to [1153](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153), [1181](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1181), [1182](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182), [1253](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1253), and [1254](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1254) of this title, enacting provisions set out as notes under sections [1153](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153), [1157](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157), [1158](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1158), [1182](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182), and [1521](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1521) of this title, and amending provisions set out as a note under sections [1182](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182) and [1255](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255) of this title] shall take effect on the date of the enactment of this Act [Mar. 17, 1980], and shall apply to fiscal years beginning with the fiscal year beginning October 1, 1979.

“(b)

(1)

(A)

Section 207(c) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) (as added by section 201(b) of this Act) [[section 1157(c) of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157#c)] and the amendments made by subsections (b), (c), and (d) of section 203 of this Act [amending sections 1152, 1153, 1182, and 1254 of this title] shall take effect on April 1, 1980.

“(2)

Notwithstanding sections 207(a) and 209(b) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) (as added by section 201(b) of this Act) [sections [1157(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157#a) and [1159(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1159#b) of this title], the fifty thousand and five thousand numerical limitations specified in such respective sections shall, for fiscal year 1980, be equal to 25,000 and 2,500, respectively.

“(3) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, for fiscal year 1980—

“(B)

for the purpose of determining the number of [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa and adjustments of status which may be made available under sections 203(a)(2) and 202(e)(2) of such Act [sections [1153(a)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153#a_2) and [1152(e)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1152#e_2) of this title], the granting of a conditional entry or adjustment of status under section 203(a)(7) or 202(e)(7) of such Act after September 30, 1979, and before April 1, 1980, shall be considered to be the granting of an[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visa under section 203(a)(2) or 202(e)(2), respectively, of such Act during such period.

“(c)

“(3)

The provisions of paragraphs (14), (15), (20), (21), (25), and (32) if section 212(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [former section 1182(a)(14), (15), (20), (21), (25), and (32) of this title] shall not be applicable to any[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who has entered the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)before April 1, 1980, pursuant to section 203(a)(7) of such Act [[section 1153(a)(7) of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153#a_7)] or who has been paroled as a[refugee](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)into the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)under section 212(d)(5) of such Act, and who is seeking adjustment of status, and the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may waive any other provision of section 212(a) of such Act (other than paragraph (27), (29), or (33) and other than so much of paragraph (23) as relates to trafficking in narcotics) with respect to such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)for humanitarian purposes, to assure family unity, or when it is otherwise in the public interest.”

Short Title of 1980 Amendment

“That this Act [enacting sections [1157](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157) to [1159](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1159) and [1521](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1521) to [1525](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1525) of this title, amending this section, sections [1151](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1151) to [1153](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153), [1181](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1181), [1182](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182), [1253](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1253), and [1254](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1254) of this title, and [section 2601 of Title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/2601), Foreign Relations and Intercourse, enacting provision set out as notes under this section and sections 1153, 1157, 1158, 1521, and 1522 of this title, amending provisions set out as notes under sections 1182 and 1255 of this title, and repealing provisions set out as a note under [section 2601 of Title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/2601)] may be cited as the ‘[Refugee Act of 1980](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/refugee_act_of_1980)’.”

Short Title of 1976 Amendment

[Pub. L. 94–571, § 1](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._94-571), Oct. 20, 1976, [90 Stat. 2703](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/90_Stat._2703), provided:

Short Title

Act June 27, 1952, ch. 477, § 1, [66 Stat. 163](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/66_Stat._163), provided that such act, enacting this chapter, [section 1429 of Title 18](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/18/1429), Crimes and Criminal Procedure, amending sections 1353a, 1353d, 1552 of this title, sections 342b, 342c, 342e of former Title 5, Executive Departments and Government Officers and Employees, sections 1114, 1546 of Title 18, sections 618, 1446 of Title 22, Foreign Relations and Intercourse, sections 1, 177 of former Title 49, Transportation, sections 1952 to 1955 and 1961 of the former [Appendix to Title 50](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/50a), War and[National](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)Defense, repealing section 530 of former Title 31, Money and Finance, enacting provisions set out as notes under this section and amending provisions set out as notes under sections 1435 and 1440 of this title, may be cited as the “[Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act)”.

“Except as otherwise provided in section 405 [set out below], all other laws, or parts of laws, in conflict or inconsistent with this Act [this chapter] are, to the extent of such conflict or inconsistency, repealed.”

“The Secretary of Labor shall issue final or interim final regulations to implement the changes made by this section to section 101(a)(15)(H)(i)(b) and section 212(n) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(H)(i)(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_H_i_b), 1182(n)] no later than January 2, 1992.”

L. 102–140, title VI, § 610](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-140), Oct. 28, 1991, [105 Stat. 832](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._832), as amended by [Pub. L. 103–416, title II, § 219](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._103-416)(l)(2), Oct. 25, 1994, [108 Stat. 4317](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/108_Stat._4317), provided that:

“(a)

The [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall prescribe regulations under title 5,[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Code, to carry out section 404(b)(1) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [act June 27, 1952, as amended, set out as a note above], including a delineation of (1) scenarios that constitute an immigration emergency, (2) the process by which the President declares an immigration emergency, (3) the role of the Governor and local officials in requesting a declaration of emergency, (4) a definition of ‘assistance as required by the[Attorney General’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=), and (5) the process by which[States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and localities are to be reimbursed.

“(b)

The [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall prescribe regulations under title 5,[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Code, to carry out section 404(b)(2) of such Act, including providing a definition of the terms in section 404(b)(2)(A)(ii) and a delineation of ‘in any other circumstances’ in section 404(b)(2)(A)(iii) of such Act.

“(c)

The regulations under this section shall be published for comment not later than 30 days after the date of enactment of this Act [Oct. 28, 1991] and issued in final form not later than 15 days after the end of the comment period.”

Savings Clause

Act June 27, 1952, ch. 477, title IV, § 405, [66 Stat. 280](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/66_Stat._280), provided in part that:

“(a)

Nothing contained in this Act [this chapter], unless otherwise specifically provided therein, shall be construed to affect the validity of any declaration of intention, petition for [naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=), certificate of [naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=), certificate of citizenship, warrant of arrest, order or warrant of deportation, order of exclusion, or other document or proceeding which shall be valid at the time this Act [this chapter] shall take effect; or to affect any prosecution, suit, action, or proceedings, civil or criminal, brought, or any status, condition, right in process of acquisition, act, thing, liability, obligation, or matter, civil or criminal done or existing, at the time this Act [this chapter] shall take effect; but as to all such prosecutions, suits, actions, proceedings, statutes, conditions, rights, acts, things, liabilities, obligations, or matters the statutes or parts of statutes repealed by this Act [this chapter] are, unless otherwise specifically provided therein, hereby continued in force and effect. When an [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=), in possession of an unexpired [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa issued prior to the effective date of this Act [this chapter], makes application for admission, his admissibility shall be determined under the provisions of law in effect on the date of the issuance of such visa. An application for suspension of deportation under section 19 of the [Immigration Act of 1917](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_act_of_1917), as amended [former [section 155 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/155)], or for adjustment of status under section 4 of the [Displaced Persons Act of 1948](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/displaced_persons_act_of_1948), as amended [former section 1953 of the former [Appendix to Title 50](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/50a)], which is pending on the date of enactment of this Act [June 27, 1952], shall be regarded as a proceeding within the meaning of this subsection.

“(b)

Except as otherwise specifically provided in title III [subchapter III of this chapter], any petition for [naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=) heretofore filed which may be pending at the time this Act [this chapter] shall take effect shall be heard and determined in accordance with the requirements of law in effect when such petition was filed.

“(c)

Except as otherwise specifically provided in this Act [this chapter], the repeal of any statute by this Act [this chapter] shall not terminate nationality heretofore lawfully acquired nor restore nationality heretofore lost under any law of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) or any treaty to which the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) may have been a party.

“(d)

Except as otherwise specifically provided in this Act [this chapter], or any amendment thereto, fees, charges and prices for purposes specified in title V of the [Independent Offices Appropriation Act, 1952](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/independent_offices_appropriation_act_1952) (Public Law 137, Eighty-second Congress, approved August 31, 1951), may be fixed and established in the manner and by the head of any Federal Agency as specified in that Act.

“(e)

This Act [this chapter] shall not be construed to repeal, alter, or amend section 231(a) of the Act of April 30, 1946 ([60 Stat. 148](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/60_Stat._148); [[section 1281(a) of title 22](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/22/1281#a)]), the Act of June 20, 1949 (Public Law 110, section 8, Eighty-first Congress, first session; [63 Stat. 208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/63_Stat._208) [[section 3508 of title 50](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/50/3508)]), the Act of June 5, 1950 (Public Law 535, Eighty-first Congress, second session [former section 1501 et seq. of title 22]), nor title V of the [Agricultural Act of 1949](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/agricultural_act_of_1949), as amended (Public Law 78, Eighty-second Congress, first session [former sections 1461 to 1468 of title 7]).”

Separability

[Pub. L. 106–313, title I, § 116](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-313), Oct. 17, 2000, [114 Stat. 1262](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1262), provided that:

“If any provision of this title [see Short Title of 2000 Amendments note above] (or any amendment made by this title) or the application thereof to any [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstance is held invalid, the remainder of the title (and the amendments made by this title) and the application of such provision to any other [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. This section be enacted [sic] 2 days after effective date.”

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, § 1(e)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–553](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-553), provided that:

“If any provision of this division [see Tables for classification] or the application of such provision to any [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstances is held to be unconstitutional, the remainder of this division and the application of the provisions of this division to any [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstance shall not be affected thereby.”

Act June 27, 1952, ch. 477, title IV, § 406, [66 Stat. 281](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/66_Stat._281), provided that:

“If any particular provision of this Act [this chapter], or the application thereof to any [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstance, is held invalid, the remainder of the Act [this chapter] and the application of such provision to other [persons](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) or circumstances shall not be affected thereby.”

Rule of Construction

[Pub. L. 117–360, § 4](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-360), Jan. 5, 2023, [136 Stat. 6293](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/136_Stat._6293), provided that:

“For purposes of this Act [see Short Title of 2023 Amendment note set out above], and the amendments made by this Act, the performance by a [crewman](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1029203033-1201680031&term_occur=999&term_src=) of ship-to-ship liquid cargo transfer operations to or from any other vessel engaged in foreign trade shall not be considered, for immigration purposes, to be [services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=), work, labor or employment by the[crewman](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1029203033-1201680031&term_occur=999&term_src=)within the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=).”

Transfer of Functions

United [States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) Information Agency (other than Broadcasting Board of Governors and International Broadcasting Bureau) abolished and functions transferred to Secretary of[State,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) see sections 6531 and 6532 of Title 22, Foreign Relations and Intercourse.

Appropriations

Act June 27, 1952, ch. 477, title IV, § 404, [66 Stat. 280](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/66_Stat._280), as amended by [Pub. L. 97–116, § 18(s)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._97-116), Dec. 29, 1981, [95 Stat. 1621](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/95_Stat._1621); [Pub. L. 99–603, title I, § 113](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), Nov. 6, 1986, [100 Stat. 3383](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/100_Stat._3383); [Pub. L. 101–649, title VII, § 705(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-649), Nov. 29, 1990, [104 Stat. 5087](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/104_Stat._5087); [Pub. L. 102–232, title III, § 308(d)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-232), Dec. 12, 1991, [105 Stat. 1757](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._1757), provided that:

“(a)

There are authorized to be appropriated such sums as may be necessary to carry out the provisions of this Act [this chapter] (other than chapter 2 of title IV) [subchapter IV of this chapter].

“(b)

(1)

There are authorized to be appropriated (for fiscal year 1991 and any subsequent fiscal year) to an immigration emergency fund, to be established in the Treasury, an amount sufficient to provide for a balance of $35,000,000 in such fund, to be used to carry out paragraph (2) and to provide for an increase in border patrol or other enforcement activities of the [Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) and for reimbursement of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and localities in providing assistance as requested by the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) in meeting an immigration emergency, except that no amounts may be withdrawn from such fund with respect to an emergency unless the President has determined that the immigration emergency exists and has certified such fact to the Judiciary Committees of the House of Representatives and of the Senate.

“(2)

(A) Funds which are authorized to be appropriated by paragraph (1), subject to the dollar limitation contained in subparagraph (B), shall be available, by application for the reimbursement of [States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) and localities providing assistance as required by the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=), to[States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and localities whenever—

“(i)

a district director of the [Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) certifies to the [Commissioner](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-535736584-1485256776&term_occur=999&term_src=) that the number of asylum applications filed in the respective district during a calendar quarter exceeds by at least 1,000 the number of such applications filed in that district during the preceding calendar quarter,

“(ii)

the lives, property, safety, or welfare of the residents of a [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) or locality are endangered, or

In applying clause (i), the providing of parole at a point of entry in a district shall be deemed to constitute an application for asylum in the district.

“(B)

Not more than $20,000,000 shall be made available for all localities under this paragraph.

“(C)

For purposes of subparagraph (A), the requirement of paragraph (1) that an immigration emergency be determined shall not apply.

“(D)

A decision with respect to an application for reimbursement under subparagraph (A) shall be made by the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) within 15 days after the date of receipt of the application.”

[[Pub. L. 101–649, title VII, § 705(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-649), Nov. 29, 1990, [104 Stat. 5087](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/104_Stat._5087), provided that:

“Section 404(b)(2)(A)(i) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [act June 27, 1952, set out above], as added by the amendment made by subsection (a)(5), shall apply with respect to increases in the number of asylum applications filed in a calendar quarter beginning on or after January 1, 1989. The[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may not spend any amounts from the immigration emergency fund pursuant to the amendments made by subsection (a) [amending section 404 of act June 27, 1952, set out above] before October 1, 1991.”
