Benefits for Certain Citizens or Nationals of Ukraine

[Pub. L. 117–128, title IV, § 401](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-128), May 21, 2022, [136 Stat. 1218](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/136_Stat._1218), as amended by [Pub. L. 118–50, div. B, title III, § 301](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._118-50), Apr. 24, 2024, [138 Stat. 913](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/138_Stat._913), provided that:

“(a) In General.—Notwithstanding any other provision of law, a citizen or [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) of Ukraine (or a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) who last habitually resided in Ukraine) shall be eligible for the benefits described in subsection (b) if—

“(1) such individual completed security and law enforcement background checks to the satisfaction of the Secretary of Homeland Security and was subsequently—

“(A)

paroled into the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) between February 24, 2022 and September 30, 2024; or

“(B) paroled into the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) after September 30, 2023 and—

“(i)

is the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of an individual described in subparagraph (A); or

“(2)

such individual’s parole has not been terminated by the Secretary of Homeland Security.

“(b) Benefits.—An individual described in subsection (a) shall be eligible for—

“(c) Clarifications.—

“(1) Nothing in this section shall be interpreted to:

“(A)

preclude an individual described in subsection (a) from applying for or receiving any immigration benefits to which such individual is otherwise eligible; or

“(B)

entitle a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in subsection (a) to lawful[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)resident status.

“(2)

Section 421(a) of the Personal Responsibility and Work Opportunity Reconciliation Act of 1996 ([Public Law 104–193](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-193)) [[8 U.S.C. 1631(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1631#a)] shall not apply with respect to determining the eligibility and the amount of benefits made available pursuant to subsection (b).

“(d) Non-Application of the Paperwork Reduction Act.—

[Chapter 35](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/44/chapter-35) of title 44,[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Code (commonly referred to as the [Paperwork Reduction Act of 1995](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/paperwork_reduction_act_of_1995)), shall not apply to any action taken to implement this section that involves translating a currently approved collection of information into a new language.”

Benefits for Certain Citizens or Nationals of Afghanistan

[Pub. L. 117–43, div. C, title V, § 2502](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-43), Sept. 30, 2021, [135 Stat. 377](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/135_Stat._377), as amended by [Pub. L. 117–328, div. M, title V, § 1501](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-328), Dec. 29, 2022, [136 Stat. 5195](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/136_Stat._5195), provided that:

“(a) In General.—Notwithstanding any other provision of law, a citizen or [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) of Afghanistan (or a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) with no nationality who last habitually resided in Afghanistan) shall be eligible for the benefits described in subsections (b) and (c) if—

“(1) such individual completed security and law enforcement background checks to the satisfaction of the Secretary of Homeland Security and was subsequently—

“(A)

paroled into the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) between July 31, 2021, and September 30, 2023; or

“(B) paroled into the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) after September 30, 2022, and—

“(ii)

is the parent or legal guardian of an individual described in subparagraph (A) who is determined to be an unaccompanied [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) under [6 U.S.C. 279(g)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/6/279#g_2); and

“(2)

such individual’s parole has not been terminated by the Secretary of Homeland Security.

“(b) Benefits.—An individual described in subsection (a) shall be eligible for—

“(1)

resettlement assistance, entitlement programs, and other benefits available to [refugees](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=) admitted under section 207 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1157](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1157)) until March 31, 2023, or the term of parole granted under subsection (a), whichever is later;

“(c) Expeditious Adjudication of Asylum Applications.—With respect to an application for asylum under section 208 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1158](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1158)) filed by an individual described in subsection (a), the Secretary of Homeland Security shall—

“(1)

conduct the initial interview on the asylum application not later than 45 days after the date on which the application is filed; and

“(2)

in the absence of exceptional circumstances, issue a final administrative adjudication on the asylum application within 150 days after the date the application is filed.

“(d) Clarification.—Notwithstanding any other provision of law, nothing in this act [probably should be “Act”, meaning div. C of [Pub. L. 117–43](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-43), see Tables for classification] shall be interpreted to—

“(1)

preclude an individual described in subsection (a), from applying for or receiving any immigration benefits to which such individual is otherwise eligible; or

“(2)

entitle a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in subsection (a) to lawful[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)resident status.

“(e) Report.—

Not later than 120 days after the date of enactment of this Act [Sept. 30, 2021], and every 3 months thereafter, the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Defense and the Secretary of[State,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall submit a report to Congress detailing the number of individuals described in subsection (a); the number of individuals receiving benefits in subsection (b), including their eligibility for benefits as[refugees](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)notwithstanding this Act; and any other information deemed relevant by the Secretary.”

Waiver of Medical Exam Requirement for Certain Afghans Seeking Admission

[Pub. L. 117–31, title IV, § 402](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-31), July 30, 2021, [135 Stat. 317](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/135_Stat._317), provided that:

“(b) Duration.—

A waiver under subsection (a) shall be for a period of 1 year, and, subject to subsection (g), may be extended by the Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) and Secretary of Homeland Security for additional periods, each of which shall not exceed 1 year.

“(c) Notification.—

Upon exercising the waiver authority under subsection (a), or the authority to extend a waiver under subsection (b), the Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) and the Secretary of Homeland Security shall notify the appropriate congressional committees.

“(d) Requirement for Medical Examination After Admission.—

“(1) In general.—

The Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Health and Human[Services,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall establish procedures to ensure, to the greatest extent practicable, that any[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who receives a waiver of the medical examination requirement under this section completes such an exam not later than 30 days after the date on which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is admitted to the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(2) Conditional basis for status.—

“(B) Removal of conditions.—

The Secretary of Homeland Security shall remove the conditional basis of the[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s status upon the Secretary’s confirmation that such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)has completed the medical examination and is not inadmissible under section 212(a)(1)(A) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1182(a)(1)(A)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182#a_1_A)).

“(3) Report.—Not later than 1 year after the date on which the waiver authority under subsection (a) is exercised, or such waiver is extended under subsection (b), as applicable, the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Health and Human[Services,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report on the status of medical examinations required under paragraph (1), including—

“(A)

the number of pending and completed examinations; and

“(B)

the number of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who have failed to complete the medical examination within the 30-day period after the date of such [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)’ admission.

“(e) Appropriate Congressional Committees.—The term ‘appropriate committees of Congress’ means—

“(1)

the Committee on Armed [Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=), the Committee on the Judiciary, the Committee on Foreign Relations, and the Committee on Homeland Security and Governmental Affairs of the Senate; and

“(2)

the Committee on Armed [Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=), the Committee on the Judiciary, the Committee on Foreign Affairs, and the Committee on Homeland Security of the House of Representatives.

“(f) Rule of Construction.—

Nothing in this Act [probably means this section] may be construed to prevent the Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=), the Secretary of Homeland Security, the Secretary of Defense, or the Secretary of Health and Human[Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)from adopting appropriate measures to prevent the spread of communicable diseases, including COVID–19, to the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(g) Sunset.—

The authority under subsections (a) and (b) expires on the date that is 3 years after the date of enactment of this Act [July 30, 2021].

Annual Report on Immigration Applications Made by Victims of Abuse

[Pub. L. 113–4, title VIII, § 802](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._113-4), Mar. 7, 2013, [127 Stat. 110](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/127_Stat._110), provided that:

“Not later than December 1, 2014, and annually thereafter, the Secretary of Homeland Security shall submit to the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate and the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives a report that includes the following:

“(1) The number of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who—

“(B)

were granted such nonimmigrant status during such fiscal year; or

“(C)

were denied such nonimmigrant status during such fiscal year.

“(2)

The mean amount of time and median amount of time to adjudicate an application for such nonimmigrant status during such fiscal year.

“(3)

The mean amount of time and median amount of time between the receipt of an application for such nonimmigrant status and the issuance of work authorization to an eligible applicant during the preceding fiscal year.

“(5)

A description of any actions being taken to reduce the adjudication and processing time, while ensuring the safe and competent processing, of an application described in paragraph (1) or a request for continued presence referred to in paragraph (4).”

Fee Increases

[Pub. L. 111–230, title IV, § 402](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._111-230), Aug. 13, 2010, [124 Stat. 2487](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/124_Stat._2487), as amended by [Pub. L. 111–347, title III, § 302](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._111-347), Jan. 2, 2011, [124 Stat. 3667](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/124_Stat._3667), provided that:

“(a)

Notwithstanding any other provision of this Act or any other provision of law, during the period beginning on the date of the enactment of this Act [Aug. 13, 2010] and ending on September 30, 2015, the filing fee and fraud prevention and detection fee required to be submitted with an application for admission as a nonimmigrant under section 101(a)(15)(L) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(L)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_L)) shall be increased by $2,250 for applicants that employ 50 or more employees in the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)if more than 50 percent of the applicant’s employees are nonimmigrants admitted pursuant to section 101(a)(15)(H)(i)(b) of such Act or section 101(a)(15)(L) of such Act.

“(b)

Notwithstanding any other provision of this Act or any other provision of law, during the period beginning on the date of the enactment of this Act and ending on September 30, 2015, the filing fee and fraud prevention and detection fee required to be submitted with an application for admission as a nonimmigrant under section 101(a)(15)(H)(i)(b) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(H)(i)(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_H_i_b)) shall be increased by $2,000 for applicants that employ 50 or more employees in the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)if more than 50 percent of the applicant’s employees are such nonimmigrants or nonimmigrants described in section 101(a)(15)(L) of such Act.

“(c)

During the period beginning on the date of the enactment of this Act and ending on September 30, 2015, all amounts collected pursuant to the fee increases authorized under this section shall be deposited in the General Fund of the Treasury.”

L. 119–4, div. A, title XII, § 11208(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._119-4), Mar. 15, 2025, [139 Stat. 38](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/139_Stat._38), provided that:

“SEC. 601. SHORT TITLE.

“SEC. 602. PROTECTION FOR AFGHAN ALLIES.

“(a) Appropriate Committees of Congress Defined.—In this section, the term ‘appropriate committees of Congress’ means—

“(1)

the Committee on Armed [Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=), the Committee on Foreign Relations, and the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate; and

“(2)

the Committee on Armed [Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=), the Committee on Foreign Affairs, and the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives.

“(b) Special Immigrant Status for Certain Afghans.—

“(1) In general.—Subject to paragraph (3), the Secretary of Homeland Security, or, notwithstanding any other provision of law, the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)in consultation with the Secretary of Homeland Security, may provide an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subparagraph (A), (B), or (C) of paragraph (2) with the status of a special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)under section 101(a)(27) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(27)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_27)), if the[alien—](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(A)

or an agent acting on behalf of the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=), submits a petition for classification under section 203(b)(4) of such Act ([8 U.S.C. 1153(b)(4)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153#b_4));

“(B)

is otherwise eligible to receive an [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa;

“(D)

clears a background check and appropriate screening, as determined by the Secretary of Homeland Security.

“(2) Aliens described.—

“(A) Principal aliens.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subparagraph if the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(i)

is a citizen or [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) of Afghanistan;

“(ii) was or is employed in Afghanistan on or after October 7, 2001, for not less than 1 year—

“(I) by, or on behalf of, the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government; or “‘(II) by the International Security Assistance Force (or any successor name for such Force) in a capacity that required the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(aa)

while traveling off-base with [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) military personnel stationed at the International Security Assistance Force (or any successor name for such Force), to serve as an interpreter or translator for such [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) military personnel; or

“(bb)

to perform activities for the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) military personnel stationed at International Security Assistance Force (or any successor name for such Force);

“(iii)

provided faithful and valuable [service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) to an entity or [organization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1178922291-1201680070&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in clause (ii), which is documented in a positive recommendation or evaluation, subject to subparagraph (D), from the employee’s senior supervisor or the [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) currently occupying that position, or a more senior [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=), if the employee’s senior supervisor has left the employer or has left Afghanistan; and

“(iv)

has experienced or is experiencing an ongoing serious threat as a consequence of the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)’s employment described in clause (ii).

“(B) Spouse or child.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subparagraph if the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(i)

is the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of a principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subparagraph (A); and

“(C) Surviving spouse or child.—

“(I) [(i)] In general.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subparagraph if the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(II)

due to the death of the principal [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(aa)

such petition was revoked or terminated (or otherwise rendered null); and

“(bb)

such petition would have been approved if the principal [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) had survived.

“(II) [(ii)] Employment requirements.—

An application by a surviving spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of a principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall be subject to employment requirements set forth in subparagraph (A) as of the date of the principal[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s filing of an application for the first time, or if no application has been filed, the employment requirements as of the date of the principal[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s death.

“(D) Approval by chief of mission required.—

“(i) In general.—

Except as provided under clause (ii), a recommendation or evaluation required under subparagraph (A)(iii) shall be accompanied by approval from the appropriate Chief of Mission, or the designee of the appropriate Chief of Mission, who shall conduct a risk assessment of the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) and an independent review of records maintained by the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government or hiring[organization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1178922291-1201680070&term_occur=999&term_src=)or entity to confirm employment and faithful and valuable[service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)to the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government prior to approval of a petition under this section.

“(ii) Review process for denial by chief of mission.—

“(I) In general.—An applicant who has been denied Chief of Mission approval shall—

“(aa)

receive a written decision that provides, to the maximum extent feasible, information describing the basis for the denial, including the facts and inferences underlying the individual determination; and

“(bb) be provided not more than one written appeal per denial or revocation—

“(AA)

that shall be submitted not more than 120 days after the date that the applicant receives such decision in writing or thereafter at the discretion of the Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=); and

“(BB)

that may request reopening of such decision and provide additional information, clarify existing information, or explain any unfavorable information.

“(II) Afghan special immigrant visa coordinator.—The Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall designate, in the Embassy of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) in Kabul, Afghanistan, an Afghan Special [Immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) Visa Coordinator responsible for overseeing the efficiency and integrity of the processing of special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visas under this section, who shall be given—

“(aa)

sufficiently high security clearance to review information supporting Chief of Mission denials if an appeal of a denial is filed;

“(bb)

responsibility for ensuring that an applicant described in subclause (I) receives the information described in subclause (I)(aa); and

“(cc)

responsibility for ensuring that every applicant is provided a reasonable opportunity to provide additional information, clarify existing information, or explain any unfavorable information pursuant to [sub]clause (I)(bb).

“(E) Evidence of serious threat.—

A credible sworn statement depicting dangerous country conditions, together with official evidence of such country conditions from the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government, should be considered as a factor in determination of whether the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)has experienced or is experiencing an ongoing serious threat as a consequence of the[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s employment by the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government for purposes of subparagraph (A)(iv).

“(F) Representation.—

An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) applying for admission to the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) pursuant to this title may be represented during the application process, including at relevant interviews and examinations, by an attorney or other accredited [representative](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-671065699-1255300052&term_occur=999&term_src=). Such representation shall not be at the expense of the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Government.

“(3) Numerical limitations.—

“(A) In general.—

Except as provided in subparagraph (C), the total number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who may be provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this section may not exceed 1,500 per year for each of the fiscal years 2009, 2010, 2011, 2012, and 2013.

“(B) Exclusion from numerical limitations.—

Aliens provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this subsection shall not be counted against any numerical limitation under sections 201(d), 202(a), or 203(b)(4) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1151(d)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1151#d), 1152(a), and 1153(b)(4)).

“(C) Carry forward.—

“(i) Fiscal years 2009 through 2013.—If the numerical limitation specified in subparagraph (A) is not reached during a given fiscal year, with respect to fiscal year 2009, 2010, 2011, 2012, or 2013, the numerical limitation specified in such subparagraph for the following fiscal year shall be increased by a number equal to the difference between—

“(I)

the numerical limitation specified in subparagraph (A) for the given fiscal year; and

“(II)

the number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this section during the given fiscal year.

“(ii) Fiscal year 2014.—If the numerical limitation determined under clause (i) is not reached in fiscal year 2013, the total number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who may be provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this subsection for fiscal year 2014 shall be equal to the difference between—

“(I)

the numerical limitation determined under clause (i) for fiscal year 2013; and

“(II)

the number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) provided such status under this section during fiscal year 2013.

“(D) Additional fiscal year.—

For fiscal year 2014, the total number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who may be provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this section may not exceed 3,000, except that any unused balance of the total number of principal[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who may be provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status in fiscal year 2014 may be carried forward and provided through the end of fiscal year 2015, notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph (C), except that the one year period during which an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)must have been employed in accordance with subsection (b)(2)(A)(ii) shall be the period from October 7, 2001 through December 31, 2014, and except that the principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)seeking special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)status under this subparagraph shall apply to the Chief of Mission in accordance with subsection (b)(2)(D) no later than September 30, 2014.

“(E) Special rule for end of calendar year 2014.—

“(i) In general.—During the period beginning on the date of the enactment of this subparagraph [Aug. 8, 2014] and ending on December 31, 2014, an additional 1,000 principal[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)may be provided special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)status under this section. For purposes of status provided under this subparagraph—

“(I)

the period during which an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) must have been employed in accordance with paragraph (2)(A)(ii) must terminate on or before December 31, 2014;

“(II)

the principal [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) seeking special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this subparagraph shall apply to the Chief of Mission in accordance with paragraph (2)(D) not later than December 31, 2014; and

“(III)

the authority to provide such status shall terminate on December 31, 2014.

“(ii) Construction.—

Clause (i) shall not be construed to affect the authority, numerical limitations, or terms for provision of status, under subparagraph (D).

“(F) Fiscal years 2015 through 2025.—In addition to any unused balance under subparagraph (D), for the period beginning on the date of the enactment of this subparagraph [Dec. 19, 2014] until such time that available special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visas under subparagraphs (D) and (E) and this subparagraph are exhausted, the total number of principal[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who may be provided special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)status under this section shall not exceed 50,500. For purposes of status provided under this subparagraph—

“(i)

the period during which an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) must have been employed in accordance with paragraph (2)(A)(ii) must terminate on or before December 31, 2024;

“(ii)

the principal [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) seeking special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this subparagraph shall apply to the Chief of Mission in accordance with paragraph (2)(D) not later than December 31, 2025; and

“(iii)

the authority to issue visas shall commence on the date of the enactment of this subparagraph [Dec. 19, 2014] and shall terminate on the date such visas are exhausted.

“(4) Application process.—

“(A) In general.—

Not later than 120 days after the date of the enactment of the [National](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2014 [Dec. 26, 2013], the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Defense, shall improve the efficiency by which applications for special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visas under paragraph (1), are processed so that all steps, including Chief of Mission approval, under the control of the respective departments incidental to the issuance of such visas, including required screenings and background checks, should be completed not later than 9 months after the date on which an eligible[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)submits all required materials to complete an application for such visa.

“(B) Construction.—

Nothing in this section shall be construed to limit the ability of a Secretary referred to in subparagraph (A) to take longer than 9 months to complete those steps incidental to the issuance of such visas in high-risk cases for which satisfaction of [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) security concerns requires additional time.

“(C) Prohibition on fees.—

The Secretary of Homeland Security or the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)may not charge an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subparagraph (A), (B), or (C) of paragraph (2) any fee in connection with an application for, or issuance of, a special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visa under this section.

“(5) Assistance with passport issuance.—

The Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall make a reasonable effort to ensure that an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subparagraph (A), (B), or (C) of paragraph (2) who is issued a special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa pursuant to this subsection is provided with the appropriate series Afghan[passport](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1216777234-1201680093&term_occur=999&term_src=)necessary to enter the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(6) Protection of aliens.—

The Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=), in consultation with the heads of other appropriate Federal agencies, shall make a reasonable effort to provide an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in subparagraph (A), (B), or (C) of paragraph (2) who is seeking special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this subsection protection or to immediately remove such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)from Afghanistan, if possible, if the Secretary determines, after consultation, that such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is in imminent danger.

“(7) Other eligibility for immigrant status.—

No [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall be denied the opportunity to apply for admission under this subsection solely because such [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) qualifies as an immediate relative or is eligible for any other [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) classification.

“(10) Annual report on use of special immigrant status.—

“(B) Content.—Each report required by subparagraph (A) submitted in a fiscal year shall include the following information for the previous fiscal year:

“(ii) The number of applications referred to in clause (i) that—

“(I)

were approved; or

“(II)

were denied, including a description of the basis for each denial.

“(11) Report on improvements.—

“(A) Requirement for report.—

Not later than 120 days after the date of the enactment of the John S. McCain [National](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2019 [Aug. 13, 2018], the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Defense, shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report, with a classified annex, if necessary.

“(B) Contents.—The report required by subparagraph (A) shall describe the implementation of improvements to the processing of applications for special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visas under this subsection, including information relating to—

“(i) enhancing existing systems for conducting background and security checks of [persons](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) applying for special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status, which shall—

“(I)

support immigration security; and

“(II)

provide for the orderly processing of such applications without significant delay;

“(ii)

the financial, security, and personnel considerations and resources necessary to carry out this section;

“(iii)

the number of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who have applied for special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visas under this subsection during each month of the preceding fiscal year;

“(iv)

the reasons for the failure to process any applications that have been pending for longer than 9 months;

“(v) the total number of applications that are pending due to the failure—

“(I)

to receive approval from the Chief of Mission;

“(II)

of U.S. Citizenship and Immigration [Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) to complete the adjudication of the Form I–360;

“(III)

to conduct a visa interview; or

“(IV)

to issue the visa to an eligible [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=);

“(vi)

the average wait times for an applicant at each of the stages described in clause (v);

“(vii)

the number of denials or rejections at each of the stages described in clause (v); and

“(viii)

the reasons for denials by the Chief of Mission based on the categories already made available to denied special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa applicants in the denial letter sent to them by the Chief of Mission.

“(12) Public quarterly reports.—

Not later than 120 days after the date of the enactment of the [National](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2014 [Dec. 26, 2013], and every 3 months thereafter, the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Defense, shall publish a report on the website of the Department of State that describes the efficiency improvements made in the process by which applications for special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visas under this subsection are processed, including information described in clauses (iii) through (viii) of paragraph (11)(B).

“(13) Report.—Not later than December 31, 2016, and annually thereafter through January 31, 2026, the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Secretary of Homeland Security, in consultation with the Secretary of Defense, shall submit a report to the appropriate committees of Congress containing the following information:

“(A) The occupations of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who—

“(i)

were provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under subclause (I) or (II)(bb) of paragraph (2)(A)(ii); and

“(ii)

were considered principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) for such purpose.

“(B)

The number of appeals submitted under paragraph (2)(D)(ii)(I)(bb) from application denials by the Chief of Mission and the number of those applications that were approved pursuant to the appeal.

“(C)

The number of applications denied by the Chief of Mission on the basis of derogatory information that were appealed and the number of those applications that were approved pursuant to the appeal.

“(D)

The number of applications denied by the Chief of Mission on the basis that the applicant did not establish faithful and valuable [service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) to the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government that were appealed and the number of those applications that were approved pursuant to the appeal.

“(E)

The number of applications denied by the Chief of Mission for failure to establish the one-year period of employment required that were appealed and the number of those applications that were approved pursuant to the appeal.

“(F)

The number of applications denied by the Chief of Mission for failure to establish employment by or on behalf of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government that were appealed and the number of those applications that were approved pursuant to the appeal.

“(G)

The number of special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status approvals revoked by the Chief of Mission and the reason for each revocation.

“(H)

The number of special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status approvals revoked by the Chief of Mission that were appealed and the number of those revocations that were overturned pursuant to the appeal.

“(14) Reports informing the conclusion of the afghan special immigrant visa program.—Not later than June 1, 2016, and every six months thereafter, the Secretary of Defense, in conjunction with the Secretary of[State,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall submit to the Committee on Armed[Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate and the Committee on Armed[Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives a report that contains—

“(A)

a description of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) force presence in Afghanistan during the previous 6 months;

“(B)

a description of the projected [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) force presence in Afghanistan;

“(C)

the number of citizens or [nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) of Afghanistan who were employed by or on behalf of the entities described in paragraph (2)(A)(ii) during the previous 6 months; and

“(D)

the projected number of such citizens or [nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) who will be employed by or on behalf of such entities.

“(15) Sense of congress.—

It is the sense of Congress that the necessity of providing special[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)status under this subsection should be assessed at regular intervals by the Committee on Armed[Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the Senate and the Committee on Armed[Services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the House of Representatives, taking into account the scope of the current and planned presence of[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)troops in Afghanistan, the current and prospective numbers of citizens and[nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)of Afghanistan employed by or on behalf of the entities described in paragraph (2)(A)(ii), and the security climate in Afghanistan.

Special Immigrant Status for Persons Serving as Translators With United States Armed Forces

[Pub. L. 110–242, § 2](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._110-242), June 3, 2008, [122 Stat. 1567](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/122_Stat._1567), as amended by [Pub. L. 117–31, title IV, § 404(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-31), July 30, 2021, [135 Stat. 319](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/135_Stat._319), provided that:

[Pub. L. 109–163, div. A, title X, § 1059](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._109-163), Jan. 6, 2006, [119 Stat. 3443](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/119_Stat._3443), as amended by [Pub. L. 110–28, title III, § 3812](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._110-28), May 25, 2007, [121 Stat. 151](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/121_Stat._151); [Pub. L. 110–36, § 1](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._110-36), June 15, 2007, [121 Stat. 227](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/121_Stat._227); [Pub. L. 110–161, div. J, title VI, § 699J](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._110-161), Dec. 26, 2007, [121 Stat. 2373](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/121_Stat._2373); [Pub. L. 112–227, § 1(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._112-227), Dec. 28, 2012, [126 Stat. 1608](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/126_Stat._1608), provided that:

“(b) Aliens Described.—

“(1) Principal aliens.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subsection if the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)—

“(A)

is a [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) of Iraq or Afghanistan;

“(B)

worked directly with [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Armed Forces, or under Chief of Mission authority, as a translator or interpreter for a period of at least 12 months;

“(C)

obtained a favorable written recommendation from the Chief of Mission or a general or flag officer in the chain of command of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Armed Forces unit that was supported by the[alien;](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) and

“(D)

before filing the petition described in subsection (a)(1), cleared a background check and screening, as determined by the Chief of Mission or a general or flag officer in the chain of command of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Armed Forces unit that was supported by the[alien.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(2) Spouses and children.—

An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subsection if the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of a principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in paragraph (1), and is following or accompanying to join the principal[alien.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(c) Numerical Limitations.—

“(1) In general.—The total number of principal [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who may be provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this section—

“(A)

during each of the fiscal years 2007 and 2008, shall not exceed 500; and

“(B)

during any other fiscal year shall not exceed 50.

“(3) Carry forward.—

If the numerical limitation described in paragraph (1) is not reached during a given fiscal year, the numerical limitation for the following fiscal year shall be increased by a number equal to the difference between the number of visas authorized for the given fiscal year and the number of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) provided special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status during the given fiscal year.

“(e) Naturalization.—

“(1) In general.—A period of absence from the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in paragraph (2)—

“(2) Period of absence described.—A period of absence described in this paragraph is a period of absence from the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) due to a [person](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=)’s employment by the Chief of Mission or[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Armed Forces, under contract with the Chief of Mission or[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Armed Forces, or by a firm or corporation under contract with the Chief of Mission or[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)Armed Forces, if—

“(A)

such employment involved supporting the Chief of Mission or [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Armed Forces as a translator, interpreter, or in a security-related position in an executive or [managerial capacity](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-835112653-1201680128&term_occur=999&term_src=); and

“(f) Application of Immigration and Nationality Act Provisions.—

The definitions in subsections (a) and (b) of section 101 of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101)) shall apply in the administration of this section.”

Battered Immigrant Women; Findings and Purposes

[Pub. L. 106–386, div. B, title V, § 1502](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-386), Oct. 28, 2000, [114 Stat. 1518](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1518), provided that:

“(a) Findings.—Congress finds that—

“(2)

providing battered [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) women and children who were experiencing domestic violence at home with protection against deportation allows them to obtain protection orders against their abusers and frees them to cooperate with law enforcement and prosecutors in criminal cases brought against their abusers and the abusers of their children without fearing that the abuser will retaliate by withdrawing or threatening withdrawal of access to an immigration benefit under the abuser’s control; and

“(3)

there are several groups of battered [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) women and children who do not have access to the immigration protections of the [Violence Against Women Act of 1994](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/violence_against_women_act_of_1994) which means that their abusers are virtually immune from prosecution because their victims can be deported as a result of action by their abusers and the Immigration and[Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)Service cannot offer them protection no matter how compelling their case under existing law.

“(b) Purposes.—The purposes of this title [see Short Title of 2000 Amendments note above] are—

“(1)

to remove barriers to criminal prosecutions of [persons](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-991716523-1485255820&term_occur=999&term_src=) who commit acts of battery or extreme cruelty against [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) women and children; and

“(2)

to offer protection against domestic violence occurring in family and intimate relationships that are covered in [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) and tribal protection orders, domestic violence, and family law statutes.”

Protection for Certain Crime Victims Including Victims of Crimes Against Women

[Pub. L. 106–386, div. B, title V, § 1513(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._106-386), Oct. 28, 2000, [114 Stat. 1533](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/114_Stat._1533), provided that:

“(a) Findings and Purpose.—

“(1) Findings.—Congress makes the following findings:

“(A)

[Immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) women and children are often targeted to be victims of crimes committed against them in the[United States,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) including rape, torture, kidnaping, trafficking, incest, domestic violence, sexual assault, female genital mutilation, forced prostitution, involuntary servitude, being held hostage or being criminally restrained.

“(B)

All women and children who are victims of these crimes committed against them in the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) must be able to report these crimes to law enforcement and fully participate in the investigation of the crimes committed against them and the prosecution of the perpetrators of such crimes.

“(2) Purpose.—

“(A)

The purpose of this section [amending this section and sections [1182](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182), [1184](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1184), [1255](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255), and [1367](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1367) of this title] is to create a new[nonimmigrant visa](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=)classification that will strengthen the ability of law enforcement agencies to detect, investigate, and prosecute cases of domestic violence, sexual assault, trafficking of[aliens,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) and other crimes described in section 101(a)(15)(U)(iii) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(U)(iii)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_U_iii)] committed against[aliens,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) while offering protection to victims of such offenses in keeping with the humanitarian interests of the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) This visa will encourage law enforcement officials to better serve[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)crime victims and to prosecute crimes committed against[aliens.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(B)

Creating a new [nonimmigrant visa](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=) classification will facilitate the reporting of crimes to law enforcement officials by trafficked, exploited, victimized, and abused[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who are not in lawful immigration status. It also gives law enforcement officials a means to regularize the status of cooperating individuals during investigations or prosecutions. Providing temporary legal status to[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who have been severely victimized by criminal activity also comports with the humanitarian interests of the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(C)

Finally, this section gives the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) discretion to convert the status of such nonimmigrants to that of[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)residents when doing so is justified on humanitarian grounds, for family unity, or is otherwise in the public interest.”

Philippine Traders as Nonimmigrants

Philippine traders classifiable as nonimmigrants under subsec. (a)(15)(E) of this section, see [section 1184a of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1184a).

Irish Peace Process Cultural and Training Program

[Pub. L. 105–319](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._105-319), Oct. 30, 1998, [112 Stat. 3013](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/112_Stat._3013), as amended by [Pub. L. 107–234, § 1](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._107-234), Oct. 4, 2002, [116 Stat. 1481](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/116_Stat._1481); [Pub. L. 108–449, § 1(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._108-449), Dec. 10, 2004, [118 Stat. 3469](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/118_Stat._3469), known as the [Irish Peace Process Cultural and Training Program Act of 1998](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/irish_peace_process_cultural_and_training_program_act_of_1998), which related to the Irish Peace Process Cultural and Training Program, was repealed by [section 2(c)(1) of Pub.
