Coordination of Amendments by [Pub. L. 104–208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208)

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, § 1(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–546](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-546), provided that:

“Except as otherwise specifically provided—

“(1)

whenever in this division [see Tables for classification] an amendment or repeal is expressed as the amendment or repeal of a section or other provision, the reference shall be considered to be made to that section or provision in the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101) et seq.]; and

“(2)

amendments to a section or other provision are to such section or other provision before any amendment made to such section or other provision elsewhere in this division.”

Applicability of Title V of Division C of [Pub. L. 104–208](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208) to Foreign Assistance

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title V, § 592](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–688](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-688), provided that:

“This title [see Effective Date of 1996 Amendment note above] does not apply to any Federal, [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=), or local governmental program, assistance, or benefits provided to an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)under any program of foreign assistance as determined by the Secretary of [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) in consultation with the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=).”

Notification to Public and Program Recipients of Changes Regarding Eligibility for Programs

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title V, § 593](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–688](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-688), provided that:

“(a) In General.—

Each agency of the Federal Government or a [State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) or political subdivision that administers a program affected by the provisions of this title [see Effective Date of 1996 Amendment note above], shall, directly or through the [States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=), provide general notification to the public and to program recipients of the changes regarding eligibility for any such program pursuant to this title.

“(b) Failure To Give Notice.—

Nothing in this section shall be construed to require or authorize continuation of eligibility if the notice under this section is not provided.”

Report on Aliens Granted Refugee Status or Asylum Due to Persecution for Resistance to Coercive Population Control Methods

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title VI, § 601(a)(2)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–689](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-689), provided that:

“Not later than 90 days after the end of each fiscal year, the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall submit a report to the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives and the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate describing the number and countries of origin of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)granted[refugee](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)status or asylum under determinations pursuant to the amendment made by paragraph (1) [amending this section]. Each such report shall also contain projections regarding the number and countries of origin of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)that are likely to be granted[refugee](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)status or asylum for the subsequent 2 fiscal years.”

Sense of Congress Regarding American-Made Products; Requirements for Notice

[Pub. L. 104–208, div. C, title VI, § 648](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._104-208), Sept. 30, 1996, [110 Stat. 3009–711](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/110_Stat._3009-711), provided that:

“(a) Purchase of American-Made Equipment and Products.—

It is the sense of the Congress that, to the greatest extent practicable, all equipment and products purchased with funds made available under this division [see Tables for classification] should be American-made.

“(b) Notice to Recipients of Grants.—

In providing grants under this division, the [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=), to the greatest extent practicable, shall provide to each recipient of a grant a notice describing the statement made in subsection (a) by the Congress.”

Improving Border Controls

[Pub. L. 103–322, title XIII, § 130006](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._103-322), Sept. 13, 1994, [108 Stat. 2028](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/108_Stat._2028), provided that:

“(a) Authorization of Appropriations.—There are authorized to be appropriated for the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)to increase the resources for the Border Patrol, the Inspections Program, and the Deportation Branch to apprehend illegal[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who attempt clandestine entry into the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)or entry into the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)with fraudulent documents or who remain in the country after their [nonimmigrant visas](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-857198958-1201680068&term_occur=999&term_src=) expire—

“(1)

$228,000,000 for fiscal year 1995;

“(2)

$185,000,000 for fiscal year 1996;

“(3)

$204,000,000 for fiscal year 1997; and

“(4)

$58,000,000 for fiscal year 1998.

“Of the sums authorized in this section, all necessary funds shall, subject to the availability of appropriations, be allocated to increase the number of agent positions (and necessary support personnel positions) in the Border Patrol by not less than 1,000 full-time equivalent positions in each of fiscal years 1995, 1996, 1997, and 1998 beyond the number funded as of October 1, 1994.

“(b) Report.—

By September 30, 1996 and September 30, 1998, the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall report to the Congress on the programs described in this section. The report shall include an evaluation of the programs, an outcome-based measurement of performance, and an analysis of the cost effectiveness of the additional resources provided under this Act [see Tables for classification].”

Report on Admission of Certain Nonimmigrants

[Pub. L. 102–232, title II, § 202(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-232), Dec. 12, 1991, [105 Stat. 1737](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._1737), directed Comptroller General, by not later than Oct. 1, 1994, to submit to Committees on the Judiciary of Senate and of House of Representatives a report containing information relating to the admission of artists, entertainers, athletes, and related support personnel as nonimmigrants under [8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(O)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_O), (P), and information on the laws, regulations, and practices in effect in other countries that affect[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)citizens and[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)resident[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)in the arts, entertainment, and athletics, in order to evaluate the impact of such admissions, laws, regulations, and practices on such citizens and[aliens,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) directed Chairman of the Committee on the Judiciary of Senate to make the report available to interested parties and to hold a hearing respecting the report and directed such Committee to report to Senate its findings and any legislation it deems appropriate.

Delay Until April 1, 1992, in Implementation of Provisions Relating to Nonimmigrant Artists, Athletes, Entertainers, and Fashion Models

[Pub. L. 102–110, § 3](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-110), Oct. 1, 1991, [105 Stat. 557](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._557), provided that:

“Section 214(g)(1)(C) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1184(g)(1)(C)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1184#g_1_C)] shall not apply to the issuance of visas or provision of status before April 1, 1992.[Aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)seeking nonimmigrant admission as artists, athletes, entertainers, or fashion models (or for the purpose of accompanying or assisting in an artistic or athletic performance) before April 1, 1992, shall not be admitted under subparagraph (O)(i), (O)(ii), (P)(i), or (P)(iii) of section 101(a)(15) of such Act [[8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15)], but may be admitted under the terms of subparagraph (H)(i)(b) of such section (as in effect on September 30, 1991).”

Commission on Immigration Reform

[Pub. L. 101–649, title I, § 141](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-649), Nov. 29, 1990, [104 Stat. 5001](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/104_Stat._5001), as amended by [Pub. L. 102–232, title III, § 302(c)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-232), Dec. 12, 1991, [105 Stat. 1744](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._1744), provided that:

“(a) Establishment and Composition of Commission.—

(1) Effective October 1, 1991, there is established a Commission on Immigration Reform (in this section referred to as the ‘Commission’) which shall be composed of 9 members to be appointed as follows:

“(A)

One member who shall serve as Chairman, to be appointed by the President.

“(B)

Two members to be appointed by the Speaker of the House of Representatives who shall select such members from a list of nominees provided by the Chairman of the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives.

“(C)

Two members to be appointed by the Minority Leader of the House of Representatives who shall select such members from a list of nominees provided by the ranking minority member of the Subcommittee on Immigration,[Refugees,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=) and International Law of the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives.

“(D)

Two members to be appointed by the Majority Leader of the Senate who shall select such members from a list of nominees provided by the Chairman of the Subcommittee on Immigration and[Refugee](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)Affairs of the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate.

“(E)

Two members to be appointed by the Minority Leader of the Senate who shall select such members from a list of nominees provided by the ranking minority member of the Subcommittee on Immigration and[Refugee](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1085535685-1201680126&term_occur=999&term_src=)Affairs of the Committee on the Judiciary of the Senate.

“(2)

Initial appointments to the Commission shall be made during the 45-day period beginning on October 1, 1991. A vacancy in the Commission shall be filled in the same manner in which the original appointment was made.

“(3)

Members shall be appointed to serve for the life of the Commission, except that the term of the member described in paragraph (1)(A) shall expire at noon on January 20, 1993, and the President shall appoint an individual to serve for the remaining life of the Commission.

“(b) Functions of Commission.—The Commission shall—

“(1)

review and evaluate the impact of this Act and the amendments made by this Act [see Tables for classification], in accordance with subsection (c); and

“(2) transmit to the Congress—

“(A)

not later than September 30, 1994, a first report describing the progress made in carrying out paragraph (1), and

“(B)

not later than September 30, 1997, a final report setting forth the Commission’s findings and recommendations, including such recommendations for additional changes that should be made with respect to legal immigration into the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)as the Commission deems appropriate.

“(c) Considerations.—

“(1) Particular considerations.—In particular, the Commission shall consider the following:

“(B)

The impact of immigration and the implementation of the employment-based and diversity programs on labor needs, employment, and other economic and domestic conditions in the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=).

“(C)

The social, demographic, and natural resources impact of immigration.

“(D)

The impact of immigration on the foreign policy and [national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=) security interests of the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=).

“(E)

The impact of per country immigration levels on family-sponsored immigration.

“(F)

The impact of the numerical limitation on the adjustment of status of [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) granted asylum.

“(2) Diversity program.—The Commission shall analyze the information maintained under section 203(c)(3) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1153(c)(3)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1153#c_3)] and shall report to Congress in its report under subsection (b)(2) on—

“(B)

how such characteristics compare to the characteristics of family-sponsored [immigrants](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) and employment-based [immigrants](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=).

The Commission shall include in the report an assessment of the effect of the requirement of paragraph (2) of section 203(c) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) on the diversity, educational, and skill level of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)admitted.

“(d) Compensation of Members.—

(1)

Each member of the Commission who is not an officer or employee of the Federal Government is entitled to receive, subject to such amounts as are provided in advance in appropriations Acts, pay at the daily equivalent of the minimum annual rate of basic pay in effect for grade GS–18 of the General Schedule. Each member of the Commission who is such an officer or employee shall serve without additional pay.

“(2)

While away from their homes or regular places of business in the performance of [services](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) for the Commission, members of the Commission shall be allowed travel expenses, including per diem in lieu of subsistence.

“(e) Meetings, Staff, and Authority of Commission.—

The provisions of subsections (e) through (g) of section 304 of the [Immigration Reform and Control Act of 1986](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_reform_and_control_act_of_1986) [[Pub. L. 99–603](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), set out as a note under [section 1160 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1160)] shall apply to the Commission in the same manner as they apply to the Commission established under such section, except that paragraph (2) of subsection (e) thereof shall not apply.

“(f) Authorization of Appropriations.—

(1)

There are authorized to be appropriated to the Commission such sums as may be necessary to carry out this section.

“(2)

Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, the authority to make payments, or to enter into contracts, under this section shall be effective only to such extent, or in such amounts, as are provided in advance in appropriations Acts.

“(g) Termination Date.—

The Commission shall terminate on the date on which a final report is required to be transmitted under subsection (b)(2)(B), except that the Commission may continue to function until January 1, 1998, for the purpose of concluding its activities, including providing testimony to standing committees of Congress concerning its final report under this section and disseminating that report.

“(h) Congressional Response.—

(1)

No later than 90 days after the date of receipt of each report transmitted under subsection (b)(2), the Committees on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives and of the Senate shall initiate hearings to consider the findings and recommendations of the report.

“(2)

No later than 180 days after the date of receipt of such a report, each such Committee shall report to its respective House its oversight findings and any legislation it deems appropriate.

“(i) Presidential Report.—

The President shall conduct a review and evaluation and provide for the transmittal of reports to the Congress in the same manner as the Commission is required to conduct a review and evaluation and to transmit reports under subsection (b).”

[References in laws to the rates of pay for GS–16, 17, or 18, or to maximum rates of pay under the General Schedule, to be considered references to rates payable under specified sections of Title 5, Government [Organization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1178922291-1201680070&term_occur=999&term_src=) and Employees, see section 529 [title I, § 101(c)(1)] of [Pub. L. 101–509](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-509), set out in a note under [section 5376 of Title 5](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/5/5376).]

Special Immigrant Status for Certain Aliens Employed at United States Mission in Hong Kong (D Special Immigrants)

[Pub. L. 101–649, title I, § 152](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-649), Nov. 29, 1990, [104 Stat. 5005](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/104_Stat._5005), as amended by [Pub. L. 102–232, title III, § 302(d)(1)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-232), Dec. 12, 1991, [105 Stat. 1744](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._1744), provided that:

“(b) Aliens Covered.—An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is described in this subsection if—

“(1) the [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) is—

“(B)

a member of the immediate family (as defined in 6 Foreign Affairs Manual 117k as of the date of the enactment of this Act [Nov. 29, 1990]) of an employee described in subparagraph (A) who has been living with the employee in the same household;

“(2)

the welfare of the employee or such an immediate family member is subject to a clear threat due directly to the employee’s employment with the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government or under a [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) Government official; and

“(3)

the principal officer in Hong Kong, in the officer’s discretion, has recommended the granting of special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status to such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)in exceptional circumstances and the Secretary of[State](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=)approves such recommendation and finds that it is in the[national](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)interest to grant such status.

“(c) Expiration.—

Subsection (a) shall only apply to [aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who file an application for special [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) status under this section by not later than January 1, 2002.

Application of Treaty Trader for Certain Foreign States

[Pub. L. 117–263, div. E, title LIX, § 5902(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._117-263), Dec. 23, 2022, [136 Stat. 3440](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/136_Stat._3440), provided that:

“For purposes of clauses (i) and (ii) of section 101(a)(15)(E) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(E)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_E)), Portugal shall be considered to be a[foreign state](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1597347259-1201680035&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in such section if the Government of Portugal provides similar nonimmigrant status to[nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)”

[Pub. L. 115–226, § 2](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._115-226), Aug. 1, 2018, [132 Stat. 1625](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/132_Stat._1625), provided that:

“For purposes of clauses (i) and (ii) of section 101(a)(15)(E) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(E)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_E)), New Zealand shall be considered to be a[foreign state](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1597347259-1201680035&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in such section if the Government of New Zealand provides similar nonimmigrant status to[nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)”

[Pub. L. 112–130, § 1](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._112-130), June 8, 2012, [126 Stat. 376](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/126_Stat._376), provided that:

“Israel shall be deemed to be a [foreign state](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1597347259-1201680035&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in section 101(a)(15)(E) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(E)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_E)) for purposes of clauses (i) and (ii) of such section if the Government of Israel provides similar nonimmigrant status to[nationals](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2045486514-1201680063&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the[United States.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)”

[Pub. L. 101–649, title II, § 204(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._101-649), Nov. 29, 1990, [104 Stat. 5019](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/104_Stat._5019), provided that:

“(2)

The provisions of paragraphs (4), (5), and (7)(A) of section 212(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1182(a)(4)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1182#a_4), (5), and (7)(A)] shall not be applicable to any[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)seeking admission to the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)under this section, and the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)on the recommendation of a[consular officer](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-293344305-1485256775&term_occur=999&term_src=)may waive any other provision of such section (other than paragraph (2)(C) or subparagraph (A), (B), (C), or (E) of paragraph (3)) with respect to such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)for humanitarian purposes, to assure family unity, or when it is otherwise in the public interest. Any such waiver by the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall be in writing and shall be granted only on an individual basis following an investigation by a[consular officer.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-293344305-1485256775&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(b)

(1) An [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) described in this section is an [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) who, as of the date of the enactment of this Act [Dec. 22, 1987], is residing in Vietnam and who establishes to the satisfaction of a[consular officer](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-293344305-1485256775&term_occur=999&term_src=)or an officer of the Immigration and[Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)Service after a face-to-face interview, that the[alien—](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(A)

(i)

was born in Vietnam after January 1, 1962, and before January 1, 1976, and (ii) was fathered by a citizen of the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)(such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)in this section referred to as a ‘principal[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=));

“(B)

is the spouse or [child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=) of a principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)and is accompanying, or following to join, the principal[alien;](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=) or

“(C)

subject to paragraph (2), either (i) is the principal [alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)’s natural [mother](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1068320061-1485255821&term_occur=999&term_src=) (or is the spouse or[child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=)of such [mother](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1068320061-1485255821&term_occur=999&term_src=)), or (ii) has acted in effect as the principal[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s [mother](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1068320061-1485255821&term_occur=999&term_src=), father, or next-of-kin (or is the spouse or[child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=)of such an[alien)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=), and is accompanying, or following to join, the principal[alien.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)

“(2)

An [immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=) visa may not be issued to an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)under paragraph (1)(C) unless the officer referred to in paragraph (1) has determined, in the officer’s discretion, that (A) such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)has a bona fide relationship with the principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)similar to that which exists between close family members and (B) the admission of such an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is necessary for humanitarian purposes or to assure family unity. If an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in paragraph (1)(C)(ii) is admitted to the[United States,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) the natural[mother](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1068320061-1485255821&term_occur=999&term_src=)of the principal[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)involved shall not, thereafter, be accorded any right, privilege, or status under the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101) et seq.] by virtue of such parentage.

“(d)

The [Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=), in cooperation with the Secretary of[State,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) shall report to Congress 1 year, 2 years, and 3 years, after the date of the enactment of this Act [Dec. 22, 1987] on the implementation of this section. Each such report shall include the number of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who are issued[immigrant](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1241937756-1201680036&term_occur=999&term_src=)visas and who are admitted to the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)under this section and number of waivers granted under subsection (a)(2) and the reasons for granting such waivers.

“(e)

Except as otherwise specifically provided in this section, the definitions contained in the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [[8 U.S.C. 1101](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101) et seq.] shall apply in the administration of this section and nothing contained in this section shall be held to repeal, amend, alter, modify, effect, or restrict the powers, duties, functions, or authority of the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)in the administration and enforcement of such Act or any other law relating to immigration, nationality, or[naturalization.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=) The fact that an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)may be eligible to be granted the status of having been[lawfully admitted for permanent residence](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2124716147-1201680062&term_occur=999&term_src=)under this section shall not preclude the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)from seeking such status under any other provision of law for which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)may be eligible.”

L. 102–232, title III, § 307](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._102-232)(l)(8), Dec. 12, 1991, [105 Stat. 1757](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/105_Stat._1757), provided that the amendment made by section 307(l)(8) to section 101(e) [title V, § 584(a)(2)] of [Pub. L. 100–202](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._100-202), set out above, is effective as if included in section 603(a) of the [Immigration Act of 1990](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_act_of_1990), [Pub. Authorization of Appropriations for Enforcement and Service Activities of Immigration and Naturalization Service

[Pub. L. 99–603, title I, § 111](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), Nov. 6, 1986, [100 Stat. 3381](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/100_Stat._3381), provided that:

“(a) Two Essential Elements.—It is the sense of Congress that two essential elements of the program of immigration control established by this Act [see Short Title of 1986 Amendments note above] are—

“(1)

an increase in the border patrol and other inspection and enforcement activities of the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)and of other appropriate Federal agencies in order to prevent and deter the illegal entry of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)into the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)and the violation of the terms of their entry, and

“(2)

an increase in examinations and other [service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) activities of the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)and other appropriate Federal agencies in order to ensure prompt and efficient adjudication of petitions and applications provided for under the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) [this chapter].

“(b) Increased Authorization of Appropriations for INS and EOIR.—In addition to any other amounts authorized to be appropriated, in order to carry out this Act there are authorized to be appropriated to the Department of Justice—

“(1)

for the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) for fiscal year 1987, $422,000,000, and for fiscal year 1988, $419,000,000; and

“(2)

for the Executive Office of Immigration Review, for fiscal year 1987, $12,000,000, and for fiscal year 1988, $15,000,000.

Of the amounts authorized to be appropriated under paragraph (1) sufficient funds shall be available to provide for an increase in the border patrol personnel of the Immigration and [Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)so that the average level of such personnel in each of fiscal years 1987 and 1988 is at least 50 percent higher than such level for fiscal year 1986.

“(c) Use of Funds for Improved Services.—

Of the funds appropriated to the Department of Justice for the Immigration and[Naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)Service, the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall provide for improved immigration and[naturalization](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1203952667-1201680065&term_occur=999&term_src=)services and for enhanced community outreach and in[-service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)training of personnel of the[Service.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) Such enhanced community outreach may include the establishment of appropriate local community taskforces to improve the working relationship between the[Service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)and local community groups and[organizations](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1178922291-1201680070&term_occur=999&term_src=)(including employers and[organizations](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-1178922291-1201680070&term_occur=999&term_src=)representing minorities).

“(d) Supplemental Authorization of Appropriations for Wage and Hour Enforcement.—

There are authorized to be appropriated, in addition to such sums as may be available for such purposes, such sums as may be necessary to the Department of Labor for enforcement activities of the Wage and Hour Division and the Office of Federal Contract Compliance Programs within the Employment Standards Administration of the Department in order to deter the employment of unauthorized[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)and remove the economic incentive for employers to exploit and use such[aliens.](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)”

Eligibility of H–2 Agricultural Workers for Certain Legal Assistance

[Pub. L. 99–603, title III, § 305](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), Nov. 6, 1986, [100 Stat. 3434](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/100_Stat._3434), provided that:

“A nonimmigrant worker admitted to or permitted to remain in the [United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=) under section 101(a)(15)(H)(ii)(a) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(15)(H)(ii)(a)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_15_H_ii_a)) for agricultural labor or[service](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=)shall be considered to be an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)described in section 101(a)(20) of such Act ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(20)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_20)) for purposes of establishing eligibility for legal assistance under the [Legal Services Corporation Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/legal_services_corporation_act) ([42 U.S.C. 2996](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/42/2996) et seq.), but only with respect to legal assistance on matters relating to wages, housing, transportation, and other employment rights as provided in the worker’s specific contract under which the nonimmigrant was admitted.”

Sense of Congress Respecting Consultation With Mexico

[Pub. L. 99–603, title IV, § 407](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), Nov. 6, 1986, [100 Stat. 3443](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/100_Stat._3443), provided that:

“It is the sense of the Congress that the President of the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)should consult with the President of the Republic of Mexico within 90 days after enactment of this Act [Nov. 6, 1986] regarding the implementation of this Act [see Short Title of 1986 Amendments note above] and its possible effect on the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)or Mexico. After the consultation, it is the sense of the Congress that the President should report to the Congress any legislative or administrative changes that may be necessary as a result of the consultation and the enactment of this legislation.”

Commission for the Study of International Migration and Cooperative Economic Development

[Pub. L. 99–603, title VI, § 601](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._99-603), Nov. 6, 1986, [100 Stat. 3444](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/100_Stat._3444), as amended by [Pub. L. 100–525, § 2(r)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._100-525), Oct. 24, 1988, [102 Stat. 2614](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/102_Stat._2614), provided for establishment, membership, etc., of a Commission for the Study of International Migration and Cooperative Economic Development to examine, in consultation with governments of Mexico and other sending countries in Western Hemisphere, the conditions which contribute to unauthorized migration to[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)and mutually beneficial reciprocal trade and investment programs to alleviate conditions leading to such unauthorized migration and to report to President and Congress, not later than 3 years after appointment of members of Commission, on results of Commission’s examination with recommendations on providing mutually beneficial reciprocal trade and investment programs to alleviate such unauthorized migration.

Alien Employees of American University of Beirut

Priv. L. 98–53, Oct. 30, 1984, [98 Stat. 3437](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/98_Stat._3437), provided: “That an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)lawfully admitted to the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)for[permanent](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-668488878-1201680094&term_occur=999&term_src=)residence shall be considered, for purposes of section 101(a)(27)(A) of the [Immigration and Nationality Act](https://www.law.cornell.edu/topn/immigration_and_nationality_act) ([8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(27)(A)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1101#a_27_A)), to be temporarily visiting abroad during any period (before or after the date of the enactment of this Act [Oct. 30, 1984]) in which the[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is employed by the American University of Beirut.”

Study and Evaluation of Exchange Programs for Graduate Medical Education of Alien Graduates of Foreign Medical Schools; Report to Congress Not Later Than January 15, 1983

[Pub. L. 97–116, § 5(e)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._97-116), Dec. 29, 1981, [95 Stat. 1614](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/95_Stat._1614), directed Secretary of Health and Human[Services,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-646160747-1201680097&term_occur=999&term_src=) after consultation with[Attorney General,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=) Secretary of[State,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-80204913-1201680099&term_occur=999&term_src=) and Director of the International Communication Agency, to evaluate effectiveness and value to foreign nations and[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)of exchange programs for graduate medical education or training of[aliens](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who were graduates of foreign medical schools, and to report to Congress, not later than Jan. 15, 1983, on such evaluation, and include such recommendations for changes in legislation and regulations as appropriate.

Adjustment of Status of Nonimmigrant Aliens Residing in the Virgin Islands to Permanent Resident Alien Status

Upon application during the one-year period beginning Sept. 30, 1982, by an[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)who was inspected and admitted to the Virgin Islands of the[United States](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2032517217-1201680101&term_occur=999&term_src=)either as a nonimmigrant[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)worker under subsec. (a)(15)(H)(ii) of this section or as a spouse or minor[child](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-94631196-1485255822&term_occur=999&term_src=)of such worker, and has resided continuously in the Virgin Islands since June 30, 1975, the[Attorney General](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-133271130-1485256779&term_occur=999&term_src=)may adjust the status of such nonimmigrant[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)to that of an alien[lawfully admitted for permanent residence,](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-2124716147-1201680062&term_occur=999&term_src=) provided certain conditions are met, and such[alien](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)is not to be deported for failure to maintain nonimmigrant status until final action is taken on the[alien’](https://www.law.cornell.edu/definitions/uscode.php?width=840&height=800&iframe=true&def_id=8-USC-92903111-1485256781&term_occur=999&term_src=)s application for adjustment, see section 2(a), (b) of [Pub. L. 97–271](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._97-271), set out as a note under [section 1255 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255).

Limitation on Admission of Aliens Seeking Employment in the Virgin Islands

L. 97–271](https://www.law.cornell.edu/rio/citation/Pub._L._97-271), set out as a note under [section 1255 of this title](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/8/1255).
